<p>OPERATIONAL DEFINITION OF TERMS AND CONCEPTS</p>
<p>Case Backlog: A case which has not been finalized or concluded within one year from the date it was filed.</p>
<p>Case Clearance Rate: The rate of resolution of cases measured by the percentage of resolved cases to the filed cases within a specified period.</p>
<p>Court Productivity: A performance measure of courts showing, on average, the resolved cases by each Judges or judicial officer in a partuclr court. Its calculated by dividing the resolved cases over a given period of time in a court, with the number of judges and/or judicial officers who served in that court.</p>
<p>Filed Case: A case that is registered or initiated in court of law for resolution in a given period.</p>
<p>Merit Productivity: Refers to productivity that is determined and calculated using merit resolutions of cases.</p>
<p>Merit Resolutions of Cases: Refers to resolved cases after a full trial culminating with a final Judgment or ruling closing the case.</p>
<p>Modes of Resolutions of Cases: A case may be resolved in various ways for instance through judgements-civil, judgements-acquittals, judgements-convictions, rulings-closing cases, sentencing at plea, withdrawals, dismissals, grant confirmed, out of court settlement, consolidation, consent recorded among others.</p>
<p>Other Case Resolutions: Are cases resolved through dismissals, sentencing at plea, consent recorded closing cases, withdrawals, out of court settlement, grant confirmed or consolidated matters which are closed.</p>
<p>Other Productivity: Refers to productivity that is determined and calculated using other modes of resolutions.</p>
<p>Pending Case: Any case which is unresolved at the end of period under reference.</p>
<p>Resolved Case: Any case where a judgment or a final ruling closing the case has been made at the end of period under reference. It also means a finalized case.</p>
<p>Time to Disposition: Time taken from filing to resolution of cases. It is given by number of days or years analyzed from filing date to resolution date.</p>
<p>3 | Page : Annual Caseload Statistics Report 2024-2025</p>
<p>Timely Submission of DCRT returns: Refers to DCRT returns sent to PMD on or before date 5th of the ensuing month. Late submission depicts non-compliance with Judiciary timelines as directed in the CJ's circulars of Oct. 2015 and Aug. 2017.</p>

<p>8 | Page : Annual Caseload Statistics Report 2024-2025</p>
<p>INTRODUCTION</p>
<p>This report provides caseload statistics from 1st July 2024 to 30th June 2025. In some instances, a brief comparison of current and previous caseload statisticshas been provided. Information on caseload is collected in courtrooms, chambers and registries by court assistants using the Daily Courts Returns Template (DCRT) and Case Tracking System (CTS). The information is then processed at headquarters by the Directorate of Strategy Planning and Organization Productivity (DSPOP) into caseload statistics and organized as diverse reports. The processed statistics are consequently used by Judiciary leadership and management to: Guide policy and administrative decisions; Track progress on Social Transformation through Access to Justice; Assess the achievements realized on programmes, projects and activities; Measure performance; Inform promotion and placement of Judges and judicial officers and, Allocate finances to courts. Further, the statistics are used by courts to make strategic decisions on measures to support expeditious dispensation of justice at court level.</p>
<p>The report is organized in court levels and further disaggregated into six thematic areas namely; filed cases, resolved cases, pending cases, case backlog, SJT implementation and, performance indicators. The presentation flows from the summary covering the entire Judiciary followed by specific statistics for the Supreme Court, Court of Appeal, High Court, Employment and Labour Relations Court (ELRC), Environment and Land Court (ELC), Magistrates' Courts, Kadhis' Courts and Tribunals.</p>
